{"parentUuid":"d10df265-af19-4122-9ad2-95cd10c0ada8","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"993bfee3-85a0-4b7f-b82a-ba53f3d6daa1","agentId":"aab6decea538aac41","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01BhDrwTPjdGuN3ecDdRsd2d","type":"tool_result","content":"And as with all things in CW, a generated answer can be edited, regenerated, or deleted. And if you find something especially useful, you can even add it as context to the task, which will inform the subsequent planning/code generation.\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/9f6402ca-fdda-461e-a8be-b34feb737bd4\" width=\"300px\" />\n\nWhen a brainstorming question is added to the task, it will show up in the task via a new section called `Ideas from brainstorming`. And while it may seem silly, we love this title so much. Why? Because it represents the notion that ideas are the output of brainstorming. And ultimately, we want CW to help you produce new and better ideas 💙\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/d56781db-ae8a-4973-bf75-d9bcf5d57af8\" width=\"300px\" />\n\nInterestingly enough, this behavior means that you can actually work on tasks with CW, without ever actually typing a task description. You simply perform brainstorming, attach the associated ideas, and then move on to the plan/implementation. However, in order for this to work well, you obviously need to be able to describe your intent or to guide CW in the direction that you want to go. So let's see how that works!\n\n#### Solution proposals\n\nIf you click the `Brainstorm` button _after_ you've typed a task description, then instead of simply getting a list of suggested questions, CW will actually present you with a proposal for how to solve your task. And this is where things get really fun 😎\n\nWhen a brainstorming question can result in multiple solutions/parts, then instead of simply answering it, CW will present you with a list of **ideas**, and allow you to select one, many, or all of them. That way, you can compose your intent by brainstorming with CW, and derive ideas through this collaborative process. Additionally, just like \"single answer questions\", you can regenerate the question to get new ideas, and then edit/refine them as needed. And as you select ideas, the `Suggested questions` will dynamically update, in order to provide you a pathway towards other interesting questions, which might be worthy of further brainstorming 🧠\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/21c3d2bb-1e2b-44ff-85ac-499e28018033\" width=\"600px\" />\n\n> Note: When you open an issue in CW, it will automatically launch the `Brainstorm` tab, and present you with the same experience as manually entered tasks. In this sense, the default `How do I solve this issue?` brainstorming question represents an alternative to the `Specification` panel, but has the benefit of being much more rich and flexible in nature.\n\n#### Asking questions\n--\nThe `Plan` panel now allows filtering it to show only the steps that were introduced in the last revision/edit (and their associated files). As a plan grows in size/complexity, this filter can make it alot easier to focus your attention on only the steps that were recently made, and therefore, would benefit from a closer review. This filter builds upon the previously-added blue dots (which indicate an \"unseen\" plan step), and represent another step towards making plan revision feel much more incremental and easy to follow :muscle:\n\n<table>\n   <tr>\n      <th>Before filtering</th>\n      <th>After filtering</th>\n   </tr>\n   <tr>\n      <td><img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/88a5e18f-cfce-4cc1-8291-d807e9e92908\" width=\"300px\" /></td>\n      <td><img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/550dc719-890f-4b43-9c65-6a6460901a00\" width=\"400px\" /></td>\n   </tr>\n</table>\n\n### Improved build/test/run inference\n\nWhen you click the `Build`, `Test` or `Run` buttons in the integrated terminal, CW will now provide better suggestions for the neccessary shell commands needed to run them. In particular, we now include any Actions workflows, package manifests (e.g. `package.json`), and the `CONTRIBUTING.md` file (if it exists) in the context, which allows CW to more properly infer the best way to build/test/run your code.\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/d0a89f46-d447-49d6-84f1-b623e41441f2\" width=\"600px\" />\n\n### Plan + implement\n\n--\nWhen you perform an NL revision against the plan, new plan steps are now annotated with a blue dot. This is meant to indicate that they are \"unseen\", and help focus your attention on the net-new changes that were made, as a result of your revision. This experience builds upon the previous change to make plan revision incremental, and we think it makes the overall iteration flow feel a lot more predictable (e.g. you don't have to try to spot what changes CW made based on your request).\n\nIn order to prevent these dots from becoming noisy, they're only visible until the next time you 1) edit the plan, or 2) perform a subsequent revision/implementation. That way, they always indicate steps you haven't \"seen\", and don't accumulate as you further iterate on your session. Additionally, the dots aren't added to plan steps you add/edit yourself. And they don't persist across browser refreshes. That way, they simply represent AI-contributed changes, that were introduced by a just-made revision 👍\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/88d2cb07-0897-46c4-b4e3-6c5c61b1b006\" width=\"400px\" />\n\n### Latest changes filter\n\nThe `Files changed` section has a new filter called `Latest changes`, which allows you to focus on the edits that were made by the most recent NL revision/implementation. This makes it a lot easier to perform iterations, and then immediately see the impact of that change (as opposed to all the changes from the session). And when combined with the new plan step indicators, this makes NL revision a lot nicer, since you can perform a revision, and then quickly spot the resulting change in both the plan and the code.\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/c15376cd-e2e1-4fba-b115-34036fda2698\" width=\"300px\" />\n\n### Devcontainer tasks improvements\n\nWhen you open the integrated terminal, the `Build`, `Test`, `Run` buttons are now always visible, even if the repo you're working against doesn't define them in a `devcontainer.json` file. And when you click any of them, CW will generate an AI-suggestion for the appropriate command(s) needed to run them (e.g. `npm run compile`).\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/d0a89f46-d447-49d6-84f1-b623e41441f2\" width=\"600px\" />\n\nIf the command looks right, then you can submit it, which will execute it in the terminal, and then persist it to the `devcontainer.json` file. You can then include this file in your PR/commit, and then all subsequent runs of that task (either build, test, or run) will be able to use this configured command in a single-click. The nice thing about this flow, is that it makes it easier for every repo to configure their build/test/run commands, without needing to remember how to do it. Simply click the buttons, and then let CW suggest and configure it for you 🚀\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/86555379-98cd-4314-bf5b-9d481dc6ff8d\" width=\"600xp\" />\n--\nThe CW extension for VS Code now allows you to generate, regenerate, revise, and implement the plan. Entirely within the editor 🔥 We still require you to **start** sessions from the CW web/mobile client, but once you have a task started, you can resume it within VS Code, and perform the most common iteration operations from there.\n\n> Note: Since this extension is early, we're still not quite ready to publish it to the marketplace. We'll likely do that in the next couple of weeks, but until them, simply hit us up in [Discord](https://gh.io/next-discord) to grab the latest VSIX 😎\n\n### URL task context\n\nWhen a task references URLs, they will now be displayed in the `Additional context` section of the `Task` panel. This ensures that you're always aware of any external context being considered, and you can control if it needed (e.g. deleting a link that is confusing the plan/etc.).\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/ce02119f-35c4-49dc-bd3e-c4c831f41e01\" width=\"400px\" />\n\n> Note: By default, CW will spider URLs that point at GitHub issues, PRs, and repo files. However, if you want it to spider external web URLs, then you need to enable the `Utilize referenced generic web content in analysis` setting in the `Experiments` dialog (underneath your avatar menu).\n\n### Cancellation improvements\n\nWhen a plan or implementation is in-progress, clicking the cancel button should now feel immediate. Additionally, if you cancel a file implementation mid-way, it will now revert the file back to its previous state (before editing it), as opposed to the previous behavior (which marked the file as `Cancelled`, and looked pretty weird). This is meaningful because when you perform an NL revision, CW automatically updates the plan and then implements it. And in order to make this UX feel delightful, we wanted to make sure you could cancel it at any time, and get the immediate/expected results.\n\n## 📅 13 September 2024\n\n- [VS Code session continuation](#vs-code-session-continuation)\n- [Incremental plan revision](#incremental-plan-revision)\n- [Improved task context](#improved-task-context)\n- [New specification UX](#new-specification-ux)\n- [Planned file placeholders](#planned-file-placeholders)\n- [Branch switching](#branch-switching)\n- [Whitespace changes](#whitespace-changes)\n\n### VS Code session continuation\n\nWe're introducing a new VS Code extension, which allows you to resume CW sessions within your editor. This allows you to start tasks from the CW web app/PWA, and after feeling good about the implementation, finish the task from the comfort of your fully-configured dev environment (e.g. using your favorite extensions, color theme, keybindings, etc.) 🤗\n\nAdditionally, this extension allows you to debug and run arbitrary client/desktop projects (e.g. mobile apps, Chrome extensions, etc.), without needing to push/pull the session's code to an intermediate branch. This works because the VS Code extension supports bi-directional file syncing with the CW service/web client. And so as you make changes in one client, they're immediately available in the other. Collectively, this allows you to start and finish work from whichever client is most convenient 😎\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/5ae9c6fb-c4de-4f4e-b37a-83b93e373c74\" width=\"700px\" /><br />\n     \n> Note: This extension is very early, and therefore, we're not publishing it to the VS Code marketplace just yet. So if you'd like to give it a try and send us feedback, hit us up on the [GitHub Next Discord server](https://gh.io/next-discord) and we'll send you the VSIX. \n     \n### Incremental plan revision\n\nWhen you perform a NL revision (using the pretty input bar at the bottom 💙), the plan is now updated incrementally, as opposed to being completely regenerated. This not only makes it faster to perform iterations, but it also makes it clearer what did and didn't change as a result of your request. To get a sense for how much nicer this feels, check out the following demo 😻\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/155e0f56-2707-44dc-98f4-9f704b119496\" width=\"800px\" />\n\n### Improved task context\n\nThe `Task` panel now includes an `Additional context` footer, which is visible when you open an issue (that has comments), or when you're working on a project that includes repository-wide instructions (e.g. a `.github/copilot-workspace/CONTRIBUTING.md` file).\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/2a8494fd-adcb-48a6-9414-658b72e62ad2\" width=\"500px\" />\n     \nThis is helpful, because it provides visibility into the external context that will be taken into account when analyzing/planning your task. Additionally, it lets you better predict and control the outcome of your session. For example, if you see a `Repository instructions` context item, then you can click it and immediately see the contents of the file (e.g. so you can know what it defines). And if you're working on an issue, that has comments you don't want included (e.g. becuase they're just \"conversational noise\"), then you can click the trash can icon next to them, and remove them consideration.\n\n### New specification UX\n\nIn order to simplify the CW workflow, we're removing the `Specification` panel from the timeline, and introducing it as optional context to the `Task`. That way, if your task description already defines the sufficient details for your intent, then you can jump straight to planning. However, if you'd like CW to help expand/ellaborate/explore on your description, then you can ask it to add a spec, and then treat that as additional input to the plan 🚀 (along with any comments and repo-wide instructions).\n\nSince this is a noticeable change, we're initially introducing it as an opt-in setting, which you can enable via the `Move specficiation to task panel` option in the `Experiments` dialog. When enabled, you'll see an `Add specification` button in the `Additional context` section of the `Task` panel. When you click that, it will generate the spec as usual, and then display a `Specification` entry in the context section for the task. If you click this, it will open the spec as a file tab, which let's you edit, revise, or regenerate the content. But with a much nicer, and full-screen view ⭐\n\n<img src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/41b2864a-3b9f-45e0-a62e-071b3b9a6412\" width=\"800px\" />\n\n### Planned file placeholders\n--\n* **File regeneration** - The file toolbar now includes a regenerate button, which allows you to ask CW to \"try again\" with implementing it. This can be useful if you've revised the plan through NL, and noticed that CW may have missed a detail. {"parentUuid":"0b9498f0-71e9-4f53-8f4c-dc3715a070dc","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"aab6decea538aac41","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01BxRN1rB2kop7MGtbzcdKu4","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"Excellent. Now I have all the research I need. Let me compile the comprehensive steerability design.\n\n---\n\n## Steerability Design for Wazir's Three Interaction Modes\n\n### Research Findings\n\n#### 1. Copilot Workspace: Edit Upstream, Regenerate Downstream\n\nCopilot Workspace organized work into a strict linear chain: **Task -> Specification -> Plan -> Implementation**. The core steerability mechanism was:\n\n- **Every layer is editable.** The spec is two bullet-point lists (current state, proposed state). The plan is a list of files with per-file step bullets. The code diffs are directly editable.\n- **Edit upstream, regenerate downstream.** When you edit the spec, the plan regenerates. When you edit the plan, affected files regenerate. The key insight: since September 2024, plan revision became **incremental** -- only the steps affected by the change are updated, not the entire plan. New/changed steps are marked with blue dots so the user can see exactly what shifted.\n- **No restart required.** You can bounce between layers at any time. Edit a file directly in the diff, or go back up to the plan, or all the way back to the spec. The system never loses completed work in layers you did not touch.\n- **NL revision bar.** A natural language input bar at the bottom lets users describe changes in plain English. The system figures out which layer(s) to update. You can scope revisions to a single file or the whole plan.\n- **Brainstorming as optional context.** Ideas from brainstorming get attached to the Task as \"additional context\" that flows downstream. This means exploration outputs feed into but do not replace the spec/plan chain.\n\n**Key takeaway for Wazir:** The cascade is layer-granular, not all-or-nothing. Editing the spec does not discard the plan -- it incrementally updates the affected parts. Copilot Workspace proved that users need to see *what changed* downstream, not just get a fresh regeneration.\n\n#### 2. LangGraph: interrupt() + Command(resume=value)\n\nLangGraph provides programmatic steerability primitives for graph-based agent workflows:\n\n- **interrupt(value)** pauses graph execution at any node, persists full graph state to a checkpointer, and surfaces the value to the caller (the user/UI).\n- **Command(resume=value)** resumes execution. The resume value becomes the return value of the `interrupt()` call inside the paused node. This is how user decisions get injected -- the node asked a question via interrupt, and the user's answer arrives as the resume value.\n- **Command(goto=node_name, update={...})** combines state mutation with routing. This is the redirect mechanism: the user can say \"skip to node X\" or \"go back to node Y\" while also updating the shared state. This is how you implement \"actually, skip the auth feature\" -- update state to mark auth as skipped, then goto the next relevant node.\n- **Multiple interrupts in sequence** receive resume values in order. You can also address them by ID: `Command(resume={\"interrupt_id_1\": \"value1\"})`.\n- **Checkpointer is mandatory.** All steerability depends on persisted state. Without a checkpointer, there is no resume.\n- **Known limitation:** `update_state` can blow away pending interrupts in some configurations. Nested subgraphs sometimes restart from entry instead of resuming from their internal breakpoint.\n\n**Key takeaway for Wazir:** The `Command(goto=..., update={...})` pattern is the critical primitive. It lets the user both **redirect flow** (go back to planning) and **modify state** (mark auth as skipped) in a single operation. Wazir needs an equivalent: a way to say \"go back to phase X with this mutation applied.\"\n\n#### 3. Ideation Team Skill: Pushing Back Into Exploration\n\nThe bladnman/ideation_team_skill implements multi-agent brainstorming with explicit steerability:\n\n- **Three actions: Plan, Ideate, Continue.** Plan is a pre-flight interview. Ideate launches the team. Continue resumes a previous session in a new versioned directory.\n- **Continue is the steering mechanism.** When you `/ideation continue <session>`, it: (1) creates a new versioned directory (never mutates the parent), (2) runs a mini-interview asking what to focus on, (3) references parent materials so the team builds on prior work. This is how you push the team back into exploration -- you explicitly continue with a new focus directive.\n- **Depth-aware convergence.** The Arbiter uses depth settings (Quick/Standard/Deep/Exhaustive) to decide when to converge vs. explore more. At Quick depth, 2-3 directions are explored. At Exhaustive, 8+. The user controls this up front.\n- **Versioned sessions, immutable parents.** Continuing a session creates `v2`, `v3`, etc. The original is never modified. This is how completed work is preserved -- it exists as a frozen session that the new session references.\n\n**Key takeaway for Wazir:** The \"immutable parent + versioned continuation\" pattern is powerful for preserving completed work. Instead of mutating the current run, a steering event creates a new \"branch\" that references the old one.\n\n#### 4. Devin: In-Thread Conversation Redirect\n\nDevin takes the most conversational approach to steerability:\n\n- **Natural language mid-task.** You can tell Devin to change direction in the chat, and it adapts, revises its plan, and keeps moving. No restart required.\n- **Timeline checkpoints.** You can scrub Devin's timeline and click \"restore checkpoint\" to roll back files and memory to a previous point. This is a full rollback -- work after that point is discarded.\n- **Take over and hand back.** You can stop Devin, make manual changes in its IDE, then resume the session and tell Devin about your changes.\n- **Dynamic re-planning (v3.0).** Devin can alter its strategy when hitting a roadblock without human intervention.\n\n**Key takeaway for Wazir:** Devin proves that natural language in-thread redirect works for simple course corrections. But for structural changes (\"skip auth\"), the checkpoint/rollback model is needed. The combination of both is the target.\n\n---\n\n### The \"Actually, Skip Auth\" Scenario: Propagation Analysis\n\nWhen a user says \"actually, skip the auth feature\" mid-execution in Wazir's current pipeline, here is what must happen:\n\n**Current state of affairs:** Wazir has no mechanism for this. The pipeline is forward-only. The user's only options are: (1) finish the run and fix it in the next run, (2) abort and restart. Both waste completed work.\n\n**What needs to happen:**\n\n1. **Identify what \"skip auth\" touches.** Auth tasks exist in the execution plan. Auth requirements exist in the spec. Auth decisions exist in the design. Auth scope exists in the clarification.\n\n2. **Determine the minimal re-run scope.** If auth is a self-contained set of tasks with no downstream dependents:\n   - Mark auth tasks as `skipped` in the execution plan\n   - No upstream re-run needed -- the spec and design are still valid, just partially implemented\n   - Continue execution with remaining tasks\n\n   If auth is deeply entangled (e.g., other tasks depend on auth middleware):\n   - Re-run planning to reorder/restructure dependent tasks\n   - Possibly re-run parts of design if the architecture changes\n   - Spec stays valid (just narrower scope)\n\n3. **Preserve completed work.** Any committed code from non-auth tasks is already on the branch. Auth-related commits could be reverted or left for later removal.\n\n---\n\n### Steerability Design for Wazir\n\n#### Core Concept: Artifact-Granular Steering with Selective Regeneration\n\nWazir's pipeline is artifact-driven. Steerability should be artifact-granular: the user edits an artifact (or instructs a mutation), and only downstream artifacts that *depend on the changed content* are regenerated.\n\n#### The Dependency Graph\n\n```\nbriefing.md\n  -> clarification.md\n    -> spec-hardened.md\n      -> design.md\n        -> execution-plan.md\n          -> task-001/ (committed code)\n          -> task-002/ (committed code)\n          -> task-003/ (not started)\n          -> ...\n```\n\nEach artifact depends on the ones above it. The steering question is always: **which is the highest-level artifact that needs to change, and what below it is invalidated?**\n\n#### Steering Operations\n\n| Operation | What Changes | Re-run Scope | Completed Work |\n|-----------|-------------|-------------|----------------|\n| **Drop a task** (\"skip auth\") | execution-plan.md | Re-validate plan dependencies only | All committed code preserved |\n| **Change a requirement** (\"use OAuth not magic links\") | spec-hardened.md | Re-run: design, plan. Affected tasks re-execute | Unaffected committed code preserved |\n| **Change the approach** (\"use approach B instead\") | design.md | Re-run: plan + execute | Unaffected committed code preserved |\n| **Add a requirement** (\"also add rate limiting\") | clarification.md | Re-run: spec-harden, design, plan, execute | All existing code preserved |\n| **Redefine the problem** (\"actually build X not Y\") | briefing.md | Full re-run | Nothing preserved (new run) |\n\n#### The Steering Protocol\n\nWhen the user provides a mid-run steering instruction:\n\n**Step 1: Classify the mutation level.**\n\nDetermine which artifact layer the change targets. Use keyword analysis:\n- \"skip/drop/remove [task]\" -> execution-plan level\n- \"change [requirement] to [alternative]\" -> spec level\n- \"use [different approach]\" -> design level\n- \"also add [new thing]\" -> clarification level\n- \"actually build [completely different thing]\" -> briefing level\n\n**Step 2: Show the impact assessment.**\n\nBefore doing anything, show the user what will be affected:\n\n> **Steering: \"skip the auth feature\"**\n>\n> **Impact:**\n> - 2 tasks removed from execution plan (task-004: auth middleware, task-007: auth routes)\n> - 1 task has a dependency on auth (task-008: protected routes) -- needs re-planning\n> - 3 tasks already completed are unaffected\n>\n> **Proposed action:**\n> 1. Mark task-004 and task-007 as `skipped`\n> 2. Re-plan task-008 to work without auth (or skip it too)\n> 3. Continue execution from task-005\n>\n> Options:\n> 1. \"Apply this change\" (Recommended)\n> 2. \"Skip all auth-related tasks including task-008\"\n> 3. \"Let me specify exactly what to change\"\n\n**Step 3: Apply the mutation.**\n\n- Write the steering event to `user-input-log.ndjson` with `type: 'redirect'`\n- Mutate the targeted artifact(s)\n- Mark downstream artifacts as `stale` (not deleted -- stale)\n- Re-run only the stale artifacts\n\n**Step 4: Preserve completed work.**\n\n- Committed code stays on the branch\n- If a completed task becomes invalid due to the steering, mark it in the plan as `invalidated` but do not revert the commit. The review phase will catch the inconsistency and flag it.\n- If the user wants clean history, offer an interactive rebase at the end (not mid-run)\n\n#### Staleness Model\n\nEach artifact gets a `_meta` header tracking its generation source:\n\n```yaml\n_meta:\n  generated_from: spec-hardened.md\n  generated_at: 2026-03-20T10:30:00Z\n  hash: sha256-of-source-at-generation-time\n```\n\nWhen a steering event mutates an upstream artifact, the system compares hashes. If the source hash changed, downstream artifacts are marked stale. Only stale artifacts are regenerated.\n\n---\n\n### How Steerability Differs Across the Three Interaction Modes\n\n#### Auto Mode\n\n**Philosophy:** The gating agent handles routine steering; user is only consulted for structural redirects.\n\n| Aspect | Behavior |\n|--------|----------|\n| **Who decides?** | Gating agent handles task-level changes (skip a task, reorder). User consulted only for scope-level changes. |\n| **Steering surface** | Escalation file (`.wazir/runs/<id>/escalations/`). Write the steering instruction there; gating agent picks it up next cycle. |\n| **Allowed without user** | Drop a task with no dependents. Reorder tasks within a dependency level. Retry a failed task with different approach. |\n| **Requires user** | Any scope change (add/remove requirements). Any design change. Any re-run of clarifier-phase artifacts. |\n| **Completed work** | Never reverted automatically. Flagged for review if invalidated. |\n| **Re-run policy** | Gating agent prefers minimal re-run. Only escalates to user if re-run scope exceeds 2 artifacts. |\n\n**User interaction point:** The escalation pause. When auto mode hits a decision it cannot make, it writes the escalation and STOPS. The user provides the steering instruction, and auto mode resumes.\n\n#### Guided Mode (Default)\n\n**Philosophy:** User approves at phase boundaries; steering happens at those natural checkpoints.\n\n| Aspect | Behavior |\n|--------|----------|\n| **Who decides?** | User at every checkpoint. Pipeline presents impact assessment before proceeding. |\n| **Steering surface** | The checkpoint itself. When the user is asked \"Does the plan look correct?\", they can say \"Actually, skip auth\" instead of picking a numbered option. |\n| **Natural steering points** | After research, after clarification, after spec hardening, after design, after plan, between tasks during execution. |\n| **Free-form input** | At any checkpoint, the user can type a redirect instead of selecting an option. The system classifies the mutation level and shows impact. |\n| **Completed work** | Shown in impact assessment. User explicitly confirms what to keep vs. invalidate. |\n| **Re-run policy** | Always shown to user. User picks: minimal re-run, full re-run from changed level, or abort. |\n\n**User interaction points:** Every existing checkpoint becomes a steering point. The change is that checkpoints accept free-form input, not just numbered selections.\n\nA new steering-specific option is added to every checkpoint:\n\n```\n5. \"Change direction -- I want to adjust scope, requirements, or approach\"\n```\n\nWhen selected, the system asks what to change and runs the steering protocol.\n\n#### Interactive Mode\n\n**Philosophy:** Continuous conversation with the pipeline. Steering happens at any moment, not just checkpoints.\n\n| Aspect | Behavior |\n|--------|----------|\n| **Who decides?** | User, continuously. The pipeline checks in more often and accepts steering at any point. |\n| **Steering surface** | The conversation itself. Any user message that is classified as a redirect triggers the steering protocol. |\n| **Proactive check-ins** | Before each task: \"About to implement auth middleware. Still want this?\" After each task: \"Auth middleware done. Anything you want to change before I continue?\" |\n| **Exploration mode** | User can say \"explore alternatives for this task\" mid-execution, triggering a mini-brainstorm before implementation. This is the ideation team pattern -- push back into exploration. |\n| **Impact preview** | Shown automatically before any steering is applied. Richer than guided mode -- includes reasoning chain and counterfactuals. |\n| **Completed work** | Full audit trail. User can see every completed task and choose per-task what to keep, invalidate, or redo. |\n| **Re-run policy** | User has full control. Can choose to re-run any individual artifact or any contiguous range. |\n\n**User interaction points:** Every moment is a potential steering point. The system:\n1. Checks every user message for redirect intent (not just at checkpoints)\n2. Offers exploration options before each task\n3. Presents \"what-if\" scenarios when the user expresses uncertainty\n\n---\n\n### What Wazir Needs to Build (Ordered)\n\n**Tier 1 -- Minimum viable steering (works within current architecture):**\n\n1. **Free-form input at checkpoints.** Every `AskUserQuestion` checkpoint should accept arbitrary text, not just numbered options. The system classifies the input and either handles it as a selection or triggers the steering protocol.\n\n2. **Steering classification function.** Takes user input, determines mutation level (task/plan/design/spec/scope), and identifies affected artifacts. Lives in `tooling/src/steering/classify.js`.\n\n3. **Impact assessment display.** Before any steering is applied, show the user what will change, what will be re-run, and what completed work is preserved.\n\n4. **Task-level skip/reorder in execution plan.** The simplest form of steering: mark tasks as `skipped` in the execution plan and continue. No upstream re-run needed.\n\n5. **Capture redirect events.** Extend `user-input.js` to handle `type: 'redirect'` with structured metadata: `{ mutation_level, affected_artifacts, re_run_scope }`.\n\n**Tier 2 -- Artifact-granular regeneration:**\n\n6. **Staleness tracking.** Each artifact gets a `_meta` block with source hash. When an upstream artifact is mutated, downstream artifacts are marked stale.\n\n7. **Selective re-run.** When artifacts are marked stale, re-run only those artifacts' generating workflows. Not a full pipeline restart.\n\n8. **Plan dependency analysis.** Understand which tasks depend on which other tasks, so that skipping a task correctly identifies tasks that need re-planning.\n\n**Tier 3 -- Mode-differentiated steering:**\n\n9. **Auto-mode gating agent steering.** Gating agent can handle task-level steering autonomously; escalates scope-level changes.\n\n10. **Interactive-mode continuous steering.** Every user message is checked for redirect intent. Proactive check-ins before/after each task.\n\n11. **Exploration re-entry.** \"Explore alternatives\" command that triggers a mini-brainstorm at any point during execution, inspired by the ideation team's Continue action.\n\n---\n\n### Relevant Files in the Codebase\n\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/skills/wazir/SKILL.md` -- Main pipeline runner, interaction modes defined at lines 297-341, checkpoints throughout\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/skills/clarifier/SKILL.md` -- All clarifier checkpoints where steering could occur\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/skills/executor/SKILL.md` -- Executor escalation pattern (lines 153-169), interaction mode awareness (lines 144-151)\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/tooling/src/capture/user-input.js` -- User input capture with types including 'redirect'\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/tooling/src/guards/phase-prerequisite-guard.js` -- Phase gates and scope coverage guard\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/skills/brainstorming/SKILL.md` -- Brainstorming skill, basis for \"exploration re-entry\"\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/skills/prepare-next/SKILL.md` -- Handoff mechanism, relevant for partial-completion steering\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/wazir.manifest.yaml` -- Phase prerequisites and workflow policy\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/docs/decisions/2026-03-19-deferred-items.md` -- Deferred items including pipeline enforcement (item 18) and interactive Claude (item 7)\n\nSources:\n- [GitHub Next -
